    (function () {
        if ( typeof window.CustomEvent === "function" ) return false;
        function CustomEvent ( event, params ) {
            params = params || { bubbles: false, cancelable: false, detail: null };
            var evt = document.createEvent( 'CustomEvent' );
            evt.initCustomEvent( event, params.bubbles, params.cancelable, params.detail );
            return evt;
        }

        CustomEvent.prototype = window.Event.prototype;

        window.CustomEvent = CustomEvent;
    })();
</script>

    <script type="application/ld+json">{"mainEntity":{"headline":"Electrochemically in situ formed rocksalt phase in titanium dioxide determines pseudocapacitive sodium-ion storage","description":"Earth-abundant TiO2 is a promising negative electrode for low-cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to its high capacity, rapid (dis)charging capability, safe operation potential and nonflammability. Crystalline anatase TiO2 is not suitable for reversible Na+ (de)intercalation, but it displays pseudocapacitive response after repeated cycles. Herein, we find and demonstrate that ordered rocksalt (RS) NaTiO2 nanograins are in situ formed by electrochemically cycling with Na+ ions in anatase and amorphous TiO2. The in situ formed RS-NaTiO2 follows a solid-solution reaction with small volume changes of only 2.0%, that determines the pseudocapacitive “mirror-like” cyclic voltammetry curve with a couple of broad redox peaks at 0.75 V vs. Na+/Na, a high capacity of 253 mAh g−1, high-rate capability and thousands of stable cycles. The multistep crystalline-to-amorphous-to-RS transformations are able to be electrochemically activated during the aging process of assembled full cells. Our finding provides a direction for developing unconventional Ti-based high-performance active materials for SIBs with both high energy and power densities. Earth-abundant TiO2 is a promising negative electrode material for low-cost sodium-ion batteries. Here, authors show that ordered rocksalt NaTiO2 nanograins are in situ formed by electrochemically cycling with Na+ ions in anatase TiO2, which determines the pseudocapacitive high-rate capability.","datePublished":"2025-02-27T00:00:00Z","dateModified":"2025-02-27T00:00:00Z","pageStart":"1","pageEnd":"9","license":"http://creativecommons.org/licenses/by-nc-nd/4.0/","sameAs":"https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-025-57310-x","keywords":["Electrochemistry","Energy storage","Materials for energy and catalysis","Science","Humanities and Social Sciences","multidisciplinary"],"image":["https://media.springernature.com/lw1200/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig1_HTML.png","https://media.springernature.com/lw1200/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig2_HTML.png","https://media.springernature.com/lw1200/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig3_HTML.png","https://media.springernature.com/lw1200/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig4_HTML.png","https://media.springernature.com/lw1200/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig5_HTML.png"],"isPartOf":{"name":"Nature Communications","issn":["2041-1723"],"volumeNumber":"16","@type":["Periodical","PublicationVolume"]},"publisher":{"name":"Nature Publishing Group UK","logo":{"url":"https://www.springernature.com/app-sn/public/images/logo-springernature.png","@type":"ImageObject"},"@type":"Organization"},"author":[{"name":"Dafu Tang","affiliation":[{"name":"Xiamen University","address":{"name":"Department of Materials Science and Engineering, Fujian Key Laboratory of Surface and Interface Engineering for High Performance Materials, College of Materials, Xiamen University, Xiamen, P.     <meta name="dc.description" content="Earth-abundant TiO2 is a promising negative electrode for low-cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to its high capacity, rapid (dis)charging capability, safe operation potential and nonflammability. Crystalline anatase TiO2 is not suitable for reversible Na+ (de)intercalation, but it displays pseudocapacitive response after repeated cycles. Herein, we find and demonstrate that ordered rocksalt (RS) NaTiO2 nanograins are in situ formed by electrochemically cycling with Na+ ions in anatase and amorphous TiO2. Our finding provides a direction for developing unconventional Ti-based high-performance active materials for SIBs with both high energy and power densities. Earth-abundant TiO2 is a promising negative electrode material for low-cost sodium-ion batteries. Here, authors show that ordered rocksalt NaTiO2 nanograins are in situ formed by electrochemically cycling with Na+ ions in anatase TiO2, which determines the pseudocapacitive high-rate capability.">

        <div class="c-article-body">
            <section aria-labelledby="Abs1" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs1">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs1-content"><p>Earth-abundant TiO<sub>2</sub> is a promising negative electrode for low-cost sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) owing to its high capacity, rapid (dis)charging capability, safe operation potential and nonflammability. Crystalline anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> is not suitable for reversible Na<sup>+</sup> (de)intercalation, but it displays pseudocapacitive response after repeated cycles. Herein, we find and demonstrate that ordered rocksalt (RS) NaTiO<sub>2</sub> nanograins are in situ formed by electrochemically cycling with Na<sup>+</sup> ions in anatase and amorphous TiO<sub>2</sub>. The in situ formed RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> follows a solid-solution reaction with small volume changes of only 2.0%, that determines the pseudocapacitive “mirror-like” cyclic voltammetry curve with a couple of broad redox peaks at 0.75 V vs. Na<sup>+</sup>/Na, a high capacity of 253 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, high-rate capability and thousands of stable cycles. The multistep crystalline-to-amorphous-to-RS transformations are able to be electrochemically activated during the aging process of assembled full cells. Our finding provides a direction for developing unconventional Ti-based high-performance active materials for SIBs with both high energy and power densities.</p></div></div></section>

                        <section data-title="Introduction"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec1-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec1">Introduction</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec1-content"><p>Electrochemical sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) arise extensive demands owing to the surge of large-scale energy storage markets and limited lithium resources<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Zhao, C. L. et al. Rational design of layered oxide materials for sodium-ion batteries. Science 370, 708–711 (2020)." href="#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e659">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Rudola, A., Sayers, R., Wright, C. J. &amp; Barker, J. Opportunities for moderate-range electric vehicles using sustainable sodium-ion batteries. Nat. Energy 8, 215–218 (2023)." href="#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e659_1">2</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="Duffner, F. et al. Post-lithium-ion battery cell production and its compatibility with lithium-ion cell production infrastructure. Nat. Energy 6, 123–134 (2021)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e662">3</a></sup>. The scalable applications of SIBs require abundant resources<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 4" title="Zhu, Z. X. et al. Rechargeable batteries for grid scale energy storage. Chem. Rev. 122, 16610–16751 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e666">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 5" title="Cai, Z. J. et al. In situ formed partially disordered phases as earth-abundant Mn-rich cathode materials. Nat. Energy 9, 27–36 (2024)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e669">5</a></sup>, e.g. Si (28.2 wt.%), Fe (5.63 wt.%), Ti (0.56 wt.%), C (0.2 wt.%), P (0.105 wt.%), Mn (0.095 wt.%) and S (0.035 wt.%) on the Earth’s crust. Seeking safe and high-performance negative electrode materials for SIBs is of significant importance but is&nbsp;full of challenges. For example, the silicon and silicon oxides are electrochemically inactive for sodium-ion storage<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="Li, Y. et al. Multilevel gradient-ordered silicon anode with unprecedented sodium storage. Adv. Mater. 36, 2310270 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e673">6</a></sup>. The conversion reaction of iron<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 7" title="Ni, J. F., Sun, M. L. &amp; Li, L. Highly efficient sodium storage in iron oxide nanotube arrays enabled by built-in electric field. Adv. Mater. 31, 1902603 (2019)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e677">7</a></sup> and manganese oxides<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 8" title="Yuan, Y. F., He, K. &amp; Lu, J. Structure-property interplay within microporous manganese dioxide tunnels for sustainable energy storage. Angew. Chem. Int. Edit. 63, e202316055 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e681">8</a></sup>, and the alloying reaction of phosphorus<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 9" title="Tian, H. J. et al. Renaissance of elemental phosphorus materials: properties, synthesis, and applications in sustainable energy and environment. Chem. Soc. Rev. 52, 5388–5484 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e686">9</a></sup> and sulfur<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Lao, M. M. et al. Alloy-based anode materials toward advanced sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 29, 1700622 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e690">10</a></sup> deliver large voltage hysteresis and poor cycling life, which is unsuitable for grid storage that requires high energy efficiency and long-term applications. Hard carbon negative electrodes display a high capacity of 300–400 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> with a low potential plateau at ~ 0.1 V vs. Na<sup>+</sup>/Na, which is advantageous for high-energy SIBs<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 11" title="Li, Y. Q. et al. Origin of fast charging in hard carbon anodes. Nat. Energy 9, 134–142 (2024)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e698">11</a></sup>. Unfortunately, its sluggish sodiation kinetics and low potential plateau give rise to the growth of Na dendrites and even serious safety risk<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 12" title="Feng, X. et al. Unlocking the local structure of hard carbon to grasp sodium-ion diffusion behavior for advanced sodium-ion batteries. Energ. Environ. Sci. 17, 1387–1396 (2024)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e702">12</a></sup>. In addition to hard carbon, Ti-based materials are abundant and have various polymorphs and derivatives, including titanium dioxides<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Wang, C. T. et al. Highly conductive hierarchical TiO2 micro-sheet enables thick electrodes in sodium storage. Adv. Funct. Mater. 34, 2301996 (2024)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e707">13</a></sup>, titanates<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="Dong, S. Y. et al. Titanates for sodium-ion storage. Nanotoday 42, 101349 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e711">14</a></sup>, titanium phosphorous<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="Xu, C. et al. Carbon-coated hierarchical NaTi2(PO4)3 mesoporous microflowers with superior sodium storage performance. Nano Energy 28, 224–231 (2016)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e715">15</a></sup>, and Ti-MXenes<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 16" title="Wang, X. et al. Pseudocapacitance of MXene nanosheets for high-power sodium-ion hybrid capacitors. Nat. Commun. 6, 6544 (2015)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e719">16</a></sup>, for use in electrochemical sodium-ion storage (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig1">1a</a> and Supplementary Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">1</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 17" title="Lou, S. F. et al. Ti-based oxide anode materials for advanced electrochemical energy storage: lithium/sodium ion batteries and hybrid pseudocapacitors. Small 15, 1904740 (2019)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e730">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="Liang, S., Wang, X., Cheng, Y. J., Xia, Y. Q. &amp; Peter, M. B. Anatase titanium dioxide as rechargeable ion battery electrode - a chronological review. Energy Storage Mater. 45, 201–264 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e733">18</a></sup>. Among them, based on the full electrochemical activation of the Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> redox couple (that is one Na<sup>+</sup> per Ti), the titanium dioxides (TiO<sub>2</sub>) display a high capacity and appropriate operation potential<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Wei, Q. L. et al. Surface-redox sodium-ion storage in anatase titanium oxide. Nat. Commun. 14, 7 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e745">19</a></sup>.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="The properties of electrochemically-driven c-a’-RS-NaTiO2 for sodium ion storage."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 1: The properties of electrochemically-driven <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> for sodium ion storage.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig1_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig1" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig1_HTML.png" alt="figure 1" loading="lazy" width="685" height="189"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-1-desc"><p><b>a</b> Operation potential <i>vs</i>. capacity profiles of Ti-based negative electrode materials for SIBs. <b>b</b> CV curves of <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> and <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> at 0.2 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. The electrochemically formed <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> nanograins display a “mirror-like” CV shape with a couple of broad redox peaks at ~ 0.75 V <i>vs</i>. Na<sup>+</sup>/Na, which is quite different from the “box-like” shape <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> electrodes. <b>c</b> GCD curves of hard carbon, NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> and <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> at 0.1 A g<sup>–1</sup>, indicating the promise of <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> for high-rate applications.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 1" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>The intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> (or Li<sup>+</sup>) into active materials requires suitable diffusion channels and empty sites<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="Viswanathan, V. et al. The challenges and opportunities of battery-powered flight. Nature 601, 519–525 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e874">20</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Zhu, X. H. et al. LiMnO2 cathode stabilized by interfacial orbital ordering for sustainable lithium-ion batteries. Nat. Sustain. 4, 392–401 (2021)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e877">21</a></sup>. Anatase TiO<sub>2</sub> (TiO<sub>2</sub>(A)) has empty octahedral vacancies for accommodating Li<sup>+</sup> ions (a radius of 0.76 Å) with a reversible two-phase transformation, displaying a flat plateau at ~1.75 V vs. Li<sup>+</sup>/Li (that is − 1.29 V vs. standard hydrogen electrode (SHE))<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="Lee, D. H. et al. Engineering titanium dioxide nanostructures for enhanced lithium-ion storage. J. Am. Chem. Soc. 140, 16676–16684 (2018)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e890">22</a></sup>. However, the initial intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> into nanosized TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) (~ 10 nm, Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">1</a>) displays an irreversible plateau at ~ 0.1 V vs. Na<sup>+</sup>/Na (− 2.61 V vs. SHE), indicating the infusing of Na<sup>+</sup> in anatase lattices requires an additional electrochemical driving force (overcoming a large potential gap of ~ 1.32 V) compared to that of Li<sup>+</sup> (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">2</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Wei, Q. L. et al. Surface-redox sodium-ion storage in anatase titanium oxide. Nat. Commun. 14, 7 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e911">19</a></sup>. Meanwhile, previous studies indicated that such intercalated Na<sup>+</sup> ions compel its near-surface anatase phase (marked as <i>c</i>) into an electrochemically formed amorphous state (marked as <i>a’</i>), which was an irreversible <i>c</i>-to-<i>a’</i> transformation<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Wei, Q. L. et al. Surface-redox sodium-ion storage in anatase titanium oxide. Nat. Commun. 14, 7 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e930">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Xu, Z. L. et al. Engineering solid electrolyte interphase for pseudocapacitive anatase TiO2 anodes in sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 28, 1802099 (2018)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e933">23</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Li, K. K. et al. Evolution of the electrochemical interface in sodium ion batteries with ether electrolytes. Nat. Commun. 10, 1248 (2019)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e936">24</a></sup>. Then, it was regarded that the near-surface <i>a’</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> reversibly reacts with Na<sup>+</sup> in subsequent cycles. Nevertheless, pristine amorphous TiO<sub>2</sub> (<i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub>), composed of distorted Ti–O polyhedra in random networks, can also be chemically synthesized (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">1</a>)<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="Wang, X. T. et al. Two-dimensional amorphous TiO2 nanosheets enabling high-efficiency photoinduced charge transfer for excellent SERS activity. J. Am. Chem. Soc. 141, 5856–5862 (2019)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e959">25</a></sup>. The distorted open channels in <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> provide continuous intercalations of Na<sup>+</sup> ions without phase transformations<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Kang, J. X. et al. Recent progress of amorphous nanomaterials. Chem. Rev. 123, 8859–8941 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e970">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Zhou, M. et al. Amorphous TiO2 inverse opal anode for high-rate sodium ion batteries. Nano Energy 31, 514–524 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e973">27</a></sup>, displaying “box-like” cyclic voltammetry (CV) curves (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig1">1b</a>) after 20 cycles<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Zhou, M. et al. Amorphous TiO2 inverse opal anode for high-rate sodium ion batteries. Nano Energy 31, 514–524 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e981">27</a></sup>. Differently, the 20 times cycled TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) electrode displays a “mirror-like” CV curve with a couple of broad redox peaks (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig1">1b</a>). The different electrochemical behaviors indicate that something rather than the amorphous structure might determine the sodium-ion storage properties after long-term cycles, but it remains largely unclear.</p><p>In this work, we reveal a multistep phase transformation from crystalline anatase to amorphous and then partially into rocksalt (RS) NaTiO<sub>2</sub> nanograins (named <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub>) during repeated (de)sodiation of TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) nanograins, as demonstrated by synchrotron X-ray diffraction (XRD) and scanning transmission electron microscopy (STEM). This electrochemically-driven phase restructuration is beneficial for in situ creating suitable diffusion channels for reversible and rapid Na<sup>+</sup> (de)intercalations. The formed RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> undergoes a solid-solution reaction with a small lattice volume change of ~ 2.0% upon Na<sup>+</sup> (de)intercalation, which determines the “mirror-like” CV curves and the sodium-ion storage capacities. The partial RS nanoregions are also observed in the cycled <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> electrode, but smaller RS regions and abundant amorphous regions lead to the “box-like” CV shape and lower capacity compared to those of <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub>. The operation potential of the <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig1">1c</a>) is between those of hard carbon and NaTi<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> negative electrodes, making it promising for both high-energy and high-power applications in grids<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Liu, H. D. et al. A disordered rock salt anode for fast-charging lithium-ion batteries. Nature 585, 63–67 (2020)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1054">28</a></sup>.</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Results"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2">Results</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec3">Electrochemical <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i> evolution of nanosized TiO<sub>2</sub>(A)</h3><p>The TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) electrode shows a continued variation in the CV curves (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2a</a>) and galvanostatic charge-discharge (GCD) profiles (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">3</a>) with reduced voltage hysteresis during the initial 20 cycles. Ex situ characterizations were performed to explore the structure evolutions during long-term cycling. Ex situ XRD patterns (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2b</a>) show the loss of crystalline diffraction peaks and the <i>c</i>-to-<i>a’</i> transformation after 1 cycle, which is consistent with previously reported phenomena<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Wei, Q. L. et al. Surface-redox sodium-ion storage in anatase titanium oxide. Nat. Commun. 14, 7 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1100">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="Li, K. K. et al. Evolution of the electrochemical interface in sodium ion batteries with ether electrolytes. Nat. Commun. 10, 1248 (2019)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1103">24</a></sup>. The destruction of long-range ordered structures after electrochemically driven Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation was further demonstrated by ex situ synchrotron-radiation pair distribution function (SRPDF) (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2c</a>), in which the correlation length decreased significantly from 50 to 16 Å after 1 cycle<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Stratford, J. M. et al. Correlating local structure and sodium storage in hard carbon anodes: insights from pair distribution function analysis and solid-state NMR. J. Am. Chem. Soc. 143, 14274–14286 (2021)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1112">29</a></sup>. The Ti K-edge X-ray absorption near edge structure (XANES) spectra (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">4a</a>) display changes in the split peaks for anatase<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="Li, J. T. et al. Revolutionizing lithium storage capabilities in TiO2 by expanding the redox range. ACS Nano 17, 21604–21613 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1120">30</a></sup> into a single consolidated peak for the amorphous state<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Xu, Z. L. et al. Engineering solid electrolyte interphase for pseudocapacitive anatase TiO2 anodes in sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 28, 1802099 (2018)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1124">23</a></sup>. Fourier transformed extended X-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) spectra reveal that the distances of first neighbor Ti–O pairs (1.54 Å) and Ti–Ti pairs (2.51 Å) expand to 1.59 Å and 2.76 Å after 1 cycle (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">4b</a>), indicating the electrochemically driven distortion and expansion of the octahedral coordination structure for accommodating Na<sup>+</sup> ions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="Hua, X. et al. Revisiting metal fluorides as lithium-ion battery cathodes. Nat. Mater. 20, 841–850 (2021)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1133">31</a></sup>.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-2" data-title="Electrochemically driven c-a’-RS transformation."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig2" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 2: Electrochemically driven <i>c-a’-RS</i> transformation.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x/figures/2" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig2_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig2" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig2_HTML.png" alt="figure 2" loading="lazy" width="685" height="527"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-2-desc"><p><b>a</b> CV curves of the TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) electrode for initial 20 cycles at 0.2 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. <b>b</b> Ex situ XRD patterns of TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) for the initial 20 cycles. The disappearance and emergence of a series of peaks indicate the <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i> phase transformation. <b>c</b> Ex situ SRPDF spectra of the TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) electrodes for pristine anatase, after 1 cycle and after 20 cycles, respectively. HRTEM images of (<b>d</b>) the pristine anatase, (<b>e</b>) after 1 cycle, and (<b>f</b>) after 20 cycles, respectively. Insets are the corresponding SAED patterns. HAADF-STEM images and inset FFT patterns of (<b>g</b>) the pristine anatase, (<b>h</b>) after 1 cycle, and (<b>i</b>) after 20 cycles, respectively. The evolutions of local atomic arrangements also indicate the <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i> phase transformation.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 2" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Notably, the diffraction peaks at 36.8°, 43.3°, and 62.5° gradually emerge after 3, 10, and 20 cycles, indicating the formation of the RS phase (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2b</a>). Moreover, the correlation length increases to 27 Å (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2c</a>), demonstrating the partial restoration of order after 20 cycles. However, the active material retains relatively less ordering compared to that of the active material before cycling. The length of Ti–O and Ti–Ti pairs decrease to 1.55 and 2.54 Å, respectively (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">4b</a> and Supplementary Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">2</a>), confirming the reorganization of the atoms and the establishment of optimized structures through 20 cycles<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 21" title="Zhu, X. H. et al. LiMnO2 cathode stabilized by interfacial orbital ordering for sustainable lithium-ion batteries. Nat. Sustain. 4, 392–401 (2021)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1231">21</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Wang, Q. D. et al. Chemical short-range disorder in lithium oxide cathodes. Nature 629, 341–347 (2024)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1234">32</a></sup>.</p><p>Ex situ microscopy characterization was further applied to investigate the microstructural evolutions (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2d–i</a>). The active material before cycling exhibits clear lattice fringes belonging to anatase phase in high-resolution transmission electron microscope (HRTEM) (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2d</a>) and high-angle annular dark field scanning transmission electron microscopy (HAADF-STEM) images (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2g</a>). After 1 cycle, it transforms into an amorphous structure, as confirmed by HRTEM (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2e</a>), HAADF-STEM (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2h</a>) and electron energy loss spectroscopy (EELS) (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">5</a>), which is consistent with previously reported results<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Wei, Q. L. et al. Surface-redox sodium-ion storage in anatase titanium oxide. Nat. Commun. 14, 7 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1260">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="Xu, Z. L. et al. Engineering solid electrolyte interphase for pseudocapacitive anatase TiO2 anodes in sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Funct. Mater. 28, 1802099 (2018)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1263">23</a></sup>. After 20 cycles, partial crystalline nanograins surrounded by amorphous regions are observed in the HRTEM image (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2f</a>). The selected area electron diffraction (SAED) pattern (inset of Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2f</a>) and HAADF-STEM image (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2i</a>) clearly display the formation of an ordering RS phase<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="Wang, Q. D. et al. Chemical short-range disorder in lithium oxide cathodes. Nature 629, 341–347 (2024)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1276">32</a></sup>, confirming the multistep <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i> transformation. The free energy and volume change for anatase- and RS-Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>TiO<sub>2</sub> were calculated based on the density functional theory (DFT) method (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">6</a>). The electrochemically-driven intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> ions into anatase causes the huge volume expansion and lattices distortions, leading to the <i>c</i>-to-<i>a’</i> transformation process. Subsequently, the free energy of RS-Na<sub>4</sub>Ti<sub>4</sub>O<sub>8</sub> is lower than that of anatase-Na<sub>4</sub>Ti<sub>4</sub>O<sub>8</sub>, indicating the energetically favorable of forming RS phase.</p><p>As the <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i> transformation is complete, the electrochemically formed RS phase remains stable (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">7a</a>), leading to well-overlapped CV curves during 20 to 100 cycles (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">7b</a>). In addition, the transforming kinetics of the&nbsp;<i>c-a’-RS</i> transformation process is controllable by regulating the cycling rates (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">8</a>) and temperatures (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">9</a>). This <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i> phase transformation is also observed when using carbonate electrolyte (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">10</a>). When the nanosized TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) is cycled in 0.5–3.0 V vs. Na<sup>+</sup>/Na to avoid the <i>c-</i>to<i>-a’</i> transformation, the crystalline anatase phase and related GCD profiles are unchanged after 200 cycles (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">11</a>). This finding underscores the necessity of forming amorphous structures for further turning into the ordered RS phase after long-term cycling.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4">Sodium-ion storage mechanism of electrochemically formed RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub>
                        </h3><p>The electrochemically formed RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> (TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) after 20 cycles) at the fully sodiated state was further investigated. Synchrotron XRD Rietveld refinement (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig3">3a</a>) indicates that all diffraction peaks are indexed to the RS NaTiO<sub>2</sub> (space group of <i>Fm</i><span class="mathjax-tex">\(\bar{3}\)</span><i>m</i>, <i>a</i> = 4.20464 Å, Supplementary Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">3</a>), which is similar to the electrochemically formed RS-Li<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Liu, H. D. et al. A disordered rock salt anode for fast-charging lithium-ion batteries. Nature 585, 63–67 (2020)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1438">28</a></sup>), RS-Li<sub>3</sub>Nb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Barnes, P. et al. Electrochemically induced amorphous-to-rock-salt phase transformation in niobium oxide electrode for Li-ion batteries. Nat. Mater. 21, 795–803 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1448">33</a></sup>) and RS-LiTiO<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Baudrin, E. et al. Structural evolution during the reaction of Li with nano-sized rutile type TiO2 at room temperature. Electrochem. Commun. 9, 337–342 (2007)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1455">34</a></sup>) phase. The average size of the as-formed RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> nanograins is ~3 nm, according to the Scherer formula<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Wei, Q. L. et al. Surface-redox sodium-ion storage in anatase titanium oxide. Nat. Commun. 14, 7 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1461">19</a></sup>. The ex situ XRD patterns of <i>c-a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig3">3b</a> and Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">12</a>) show slight shifts in the diffraction peaks during desodiation and then sodiation, which is a solid-solution reaction mechanism. The changes in the diffraction peaks imply a very small volume change of ~ 2.0% (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">12</a>), which is also confirmed by the unchanged ex situ SAED patterns (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">13</a>). Ex situ Ti L-edge EELS spectra (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">14</a>) and Ti 2<i>p</i> X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig3">3c</a> and Supplementary Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">4</a>) support the reversible redox couple of Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup> during (de)sodiation. The sodiated sample has an average Ti valance of + 3.05, which is close to that of + 3 in RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub>. After desodiation, the average Ti valance increases to + 3.75, indicating ~ 0.7 Na<sup>+</sup> per Ti (corresponding to 234.5 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>), which is close to the reversible capacity of 253 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 20 cycles (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">3a</a>). The residual Na<sup>+</sup> ions help to stabilize the RS phase. In addition, RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> maintains diffraction peaks after 61 days of air exposure, indicating its air stability (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">15</a>).</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="Sodium-ion storage of RS-NaTiO2."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 3: Sodium-ion storage of RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub>.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x/figures/3" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig3_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig3" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig3_HTML.png" alt="figure 3" loading="lazy" width="685" height="559"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-3-desc"><p><b>a</b> Rietveld refinement synchrotron XRD pattern of <i>c-a’-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> (TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) after 20 cycles) at the fully sodiated state. <b>b</b> Ex situ XRD patterns and (<b>c</b>) ex situ XPS spectra of <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> at different potentials, indicating a solid-solution (de)sodiation process. <b>d</b> STEM image, (<b>e</b>) schematic atomic configuration of the RS phase, (<b>f</b>) FFT pattern, and (<b>g</b>) Ti and Na element mapping of the fully sodiated <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub>. <b>h</b> Atomic position distribution spectra from (<b>g</b>). <b>i</b> Schematic of the sodium-ion storage mechanism: the electrochemically driven <i>c-a’-RS</i> transformation and the solid-solution reaction of in situ formed RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> nanograins during cycling with Na<sup>+</sup>.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x/figures/3" data-track-dest="link:Figure3 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 3" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>An ex situ HAADF-STEM image (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig3">3d</a>) illustrates the coexistence of the crystalline RS NaTiO<sub>2</sub> nanograins and amorphous regions. The schematic atomic configuration (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig3">3e</a>) and fast Fourier transform (FFT) pattern (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig3">3f</a>) along the crystallographic zone axis of [<span class="mathjax-tex">\(\bar{1}\)</span>10] clearly show the RS lattices. Atomic-resolution X-ray energy disperses spectroscopy (EDS) mapping (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig3">3g</a>) reveals no correlations between the Na and Ti signals in different directions (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig3">3h</a> and Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">16</a>), implying cation-disordering of the Na and Ti atoms at the octahedral (4a) sites. The octahedral sites are occupied by Na<sup>+</sup> ions for sodiated RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub>, while the vacancies remain after desodiation. The overall electrochemically driven structural evolutions of nanosized TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) during cycling with Na<sup>+</sup> ions are schematically summarized in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig3">3i</a>. The initial intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> into anatase causes a <i>c</i>-to-<i>a’</i> transformation, leading to a decrease in long-range order. Scrutinizing the continued changes in the CV curves (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2a</a>), the anodic peak first emerged at the 2nd cycle during the extraction of Na<sup>+</sup> from the sodiated materials. This phenomenon indicates the initial formation of RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> when the Na<sup>+</sup> ions occupy the octahedral sites. Upon repeated cycles with Na<sup>+</sup> ions, the distorted Ti–O octahedra are continuously rearranged, leading to the continued formation of RS nanograins. The reversible Na<sup>+</sup> extraction and intercalation between the RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> and RS-Na<sub>1-<i>x</i></sub>TiO<sub>2</sub> follow a solid-solution reaction with the redox of Ti<sup>4+</sup>/Ti<sup>3+</sup>, finally leading to “mirror-like” CV curves with broad redox peaks.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5">Electrochemical <i>a</i>-to-<i>RS</i> evolution of <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub>
                        </h3><p>To determine the origins of the differences in the electrochemical properties between cycled TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) and <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig1">1b</a>), detailed ex situ XRD, SRPDF and STEM characterizations of <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> were also conducted, as shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4</a>. The <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> electrode shows a “box-like” CV curve for the 1st cycle (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4a</a>), which is different from the initial <i>c</i>-to-<i>a’</i> of TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2a</a>). There are no significant redox peaks during the initial 10 cycles, which is consistent with the previously reported <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> arrays<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Zhou, M. et al. Amorphous TiO2 inverse opal anode for high-rate sodium ion batteries. Nano Energy 31, 514–524 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1775">27</a></sup> and spheres<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 35" title="Deng, C. J. et al. Amorphous and crystalline TiO2 nanoparticle negative electrodes for sodium-ion batteries. Electrochim. Acta. 321, 134723 (2019)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1780">35</a></sup>. Even after 20 cycles, only small broad peaks emerge at ~ 0.75 V vs. Na<sup>+</sup>/Na (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4a</a>). EXAFS spectra (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">17</a> and Supplementary Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">5</a>) reveal that the distance of the first neighbor Ti–O and Ti–Ti pairs are 1.60 and 2.69 Å, respectively, which are larger than those of crystalline anatase (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">4</a>). The large Ti–O polyhedra in <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> accommodate Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation, leading to the “box-like” CV curve at the 1st cycle. After 20 cycles, the Ti–O and Ti–Ti pairs are shortened to 1.56 Å and 2.55 Å, respectively. Ex situ SRPDF spectra (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4b</a>) reveal a continuous extension of the correlation length from 7 Å (before cycling) to 9 Å (after 1 cycle) and then to 12 Å (after 20 cycles), suggesting an increase in long-range order. However, laboratory X-ray did not detect diffraction patterns from the in situ formed RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> nanograins for <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> after cycling (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4c</a>). Ex situ TEM and STEM were further performed (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4d–i</a>). The chemically synthesized active material before cycling is amorphous (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4d, g</a>). After cycling with Na<sup>+</sup>, the RS nanograins and amorphous regions are observed (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4e, f</a>). The amorphous to RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> (<i>a-to-RS</i>) phase transformation is confirmed by diffraction rings in the SAED pattern (insets of Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4e, f</a>) and atom arrangements in the STEM image (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4h, i</a>).</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-4" data-title="Electrochemical structural evolution of a-TiO2 after cycling."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig4" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 4: Electrochemical structural evolution of <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> after cycling.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x/figures/4" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig4_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig4" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig4_HTML.png" alt="figure 4" loading="lazy" width="685" height="529"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-4-desc"><p><b>a</b> Consecutive CV curves of <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> electrode for initial 20 cycles at 0.2 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. <b>b</b> Ex situ SRPDF spectra of the pristine <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub>, after 1 and 20 cycles. <b>c</b> Ex situ XRD patterns of <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> during 20 cycles. HRTEM images of (<b>d</b>) pristine <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub>, (<b>e</b>) after 1 cycle, and (<b>f</b>) after 20 cycles, respectively. The insets are the corresponding SAED patterns. Atomic-resolution HAADF-STEM images and the inset FFT patterns of (<b>g</b>) the pristine <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub>, (<b>h</b>) after 1 cycle, and (<b>i</b>) after 20 cycles. The <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> also partially transforms into RS nanograins after cycling with Na<sup>+</sup>.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x/figures/4" data-track-dest="link:Figure4 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 4" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>The <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> undergoes a transformation to the RS phase after 1 cycle, which is attributed to the pristine amorphous nature of <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> with disordered Ti–O polyhedra<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Kang, J. X. et al. Recent progress of amorphous nanomaterials. Chem. Rev. 123, 8859–8941 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1945">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Barnes, P. et al. Electrochemically induced amorphous-to-rock-salt phase transformation in niobium oxide electrode for Li-ion batteries. Nat. Mater. 21, 795–803 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1948">33</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 36" title="Gao, Q. et al. Direct evidence of lithium-induced atomic ordering in amorphous TiO2 nanotubes. Chem. Mater. 26, 1660–1669 (2014)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1951">36</a></sup>. However, the correlation length of 12 Å for cycled <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> is shorter than that of 27 Å for cycled TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">18</a>), indicating that the <i>a</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> (cycled <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> with formed RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub>) electrode has much smaller ordered domains than the <i>c-a’-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrode<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="Zheng, T., Hu, P. F., Wang, Z. C. &amp; Guo, T. Q. 2D amorphous iron selenide sulfide nanosheets for stable and rapid sodium-ion storage. Adv. Mater. 35, 2306577 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e1988">37</a></sup>, which is consistent with the ex situ XRD results (Figs.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2b</a> and <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4c</a>). In contrast to the <i>a-to-RS</i> transformation of chemically synthesized <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> with random Ti–O networks, the in situ multistep <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i> transformation from the ordered Ti–O octahedra in TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) results in larger RS nanograins than those in cycled <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub>, which significantly affects their sodium-ion storage properties<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Kang, J. X. et al. Recent progress of amorphous nanomaterials. Chem. Rev. 123, 8859–8941 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2024">26</a></sup>.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6">Sodium-ion storage performance of electrochemically in situ formed RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub>
                        </h3><p>The <i>c-a’-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> displays a “mirror-like” CV curve with a couple of broad peaks (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5a</a>), whereas <i>a-</i>RS<i>-</i>NaTiO<sub>2</sub> displays a “box-like” shape (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5b</a>). Using <i>i </i>= a<i>v</i><sup><i>b</i></sup> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Wei, Q. L. et al. Surface-redox sodium-ion storage in anatase titanium oxide. Nat. Commun. 14, 7 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2068">19</a></sup>), the fitted <i>b</i>-values of the two electrodes are both equal to 1.0 (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">19a–d</a>). Meanwhile, the simulated capacitive contribution<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="Wang, C. T. et al. Highly conductive hierarchical TiO2 micro-sheet enables thick electrodes in sodium storage. Adv. Funct. Mater. 34, 2301996 (2024)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2079">13</a></sup> of <i>c-a’-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> and <i>a-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrodes are 92.4% and 88.6% at 1.0 mV s<sup>–1</sup> (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">19e, f</a>), respectively. The kinetics analysis indicates pseudocapacitive behavior of the RS and amorphous regions. The main distinctions between the <i>c-a’-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> and <i>a-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrodes are their sizes of RS nanograins and residual amorphous regions. It has been reported that electrochemically formed RS-Li<sub>3</sub>Nb<sub>2</sub>O<sub>5</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="Barnes, P. et al. Electrochemically induced amorphous-to-rock-salt phase transformation in niobium oxide electrode for Li-ion batteries. Nat. Mater. 21, 795–803 (2022)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2116">33</a></sup>) and RS-LiTiO<sub>2</sub> (ref. <sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 34" title="Baudrin, E. et al. Structural evolution during the reaction of Li with nano-sized rutile type TiO2 at room temperature. Electrochem. Commun. 9, 337–342 (2007)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2123">34</a></sup>) displayed analogous “mirror-like” d<i>Q</i>/d<i>V</i> profiles according to their solid solution reactions with small voltage hysteresis, which is consistent with the electrochemical properties of RS-NaTiO<sub>2</sub>. The measured response currents are mainly derived from the RS nanograins and amorphous regions (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">20</a>). The capacity contributions from RS nanograins and amorphous regions at different cycles are further analyzed (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">21a–f</a>). The capacity contribution from RS nanograins gradually increases from 34.1% at the 3rd cycle (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">21a, b</a>), to 56.4% at the 10th cycle (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">21c, d</a>), and to 70% at the 20th cycle (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">21e, f</a>), suggesting the growth of RS nanograins during cycling with Na<sup>+</sup>. After 20 cycles, the RS nanograins get stable. Owing to the smaller RS nanograins and more residual amorphous regions in the&nbsp;<i>a-RS-</i>NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrode (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig4">4f</a> and inset of Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5b</a>), it displays the “box-like” CV curves (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5b</a>). However, the <i>c-a’-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrode has large and abundant RS nanograins (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig2">2f</a> and inset of Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5a</a>), displaying broad redox peaks from the solid-solution reaction of the RS phase with small voltage hysteresis (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5a</a>).</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-5" data-title="Electrochemical performance of the c-a’-RS-NaTiO2 and a-RS-NaTiO2 electrodes."><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig5" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig. 5: Electrochemical performance of the <i>c-a’-RS-</i>NaTiO<sub>2</sub> and <i>a-RS-</i>NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrodes.</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x/figures/5" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig5_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig5" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1038%2Fs41467-025-57310-x/MediaObjects/41467_2025_57310_Fig5_HTML.png" alt="figure 5" loading="lazy" width="685" height="359"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-5-desc"><p>Deconvolution of the CV curves for (<b>a</b>) the <i>c-a’-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> and (<b>b</b>) <i>a-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrodes at 0.2 mV s<sup>–1</sup>. <b>c</b> Rate performance and (<b>d</b>) cycling performances of the <i>c-a’-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> and <i>a-RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrodes. <b>e</b> GITT curves and corresponding logarithm <i>D</i><sub>Na</sub><sup>+</sup> <i>vs</i>. Na<sub><i>x</i></sub>TiO<sub>2</sub> plots of <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> and (<b>f</b>) TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) electrodes for the 1st, 2nd and 20th sodiation processes. The in situ-formed RS nanograins display fast Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion abilities.</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x/figures/5" data-track-dest="link:Figure5 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 5" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>The rate and cycling performance of the <i>a-RS-</i>NaTiO<sub>2</sub> and <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrodes are further discussed in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5c, d</a>. The <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> and TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) electrodes deliver close initial sodiation capacities. However, during 2 − 20 cycles, <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub> delivers a much lower capacity and quicker capacity fading, which is attributed to the irreversible reaction of the chemically synthesized amorphous materials with lots of defects<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Kang, J. X. et al. Recent progress of amorphous nanomaterials. Chem. Rev. 123, 8859–8941 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2317">26</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="Zhou, M. et al. Amorphous TiO2 inverse opal anode for high-rate sodium ion batteries. Nano Energy 31, 514–524 (2017)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2320">27</a></sup>. When the RS nanograins get stable after 20 pre-cycles, the <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrode delivers 253, 224, and 200 mAh g<sup>–1</sup> at 0.1, 1.0, and 4.0 A g<sup>–1</sup>, respectively, which are superior to those of the <i>a</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrode (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5c</a>). In addition, the <i>c</i>-<i>a’</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrode delivers capacity retention of 72% after 5000 cycles at 2 A g<sup>–1</sup> (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5d</a>), which is better than that of 49% for the <i>a</i>-<i>RS</i>-NaTiO<sub>2</sub> electrode.</p><p>The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) was employed to investigate the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusivity before and after cycling<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 38" title="Chien, Y. C. et al. Rapid determination of solid-state diffusion coefficients in Li-based batteries via intermittent current interruption method. Nat. Commun. 14, 2289 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2382">38</a></sup>. Relying on the open frameworks in <i>a</i>-TiO<sub>2</sub>, the diffusion coefficient is 10<sup>–10</sup> ~ 10<sup>–11</sup> cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> and remains relatively unchanged during 20 cycles (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5e</a>). In contrast, the initial intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> into TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) accompanied by the <i>c</i>-to-<i>a’</i> transformation has a low Na<sup>+</sup> diffusivity of 10<sup>–15</sup> ~ 10<sup>–16</sup>cm <sup>2</sup><sup>–1</sup>. After partial transformation into the RS phase, the apparent Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient increases dramatically by five orders of magnitude up to 10<sup>–10 </sup>cm<sup>2</sup> s<sup>–1</sup> (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5f</a>), which is related to its high-rate capability. Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) results of TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) during the initial 20 cycles show stable SEI resistance (<i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub>) and decreased charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) for the subsequent <i>a’-RS</i> transformation (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">22</a> and Supplementary Table&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">6</a>), confirming the enhanced kinetics by the in situ formation of RS phase. Previous works reported that TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) nanomaterials displayed surface-dependent specific capacities, which were determined by the ~ 5 nm thickness of near-surface activation regions<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Song, G. R. et al. Physical interpretations of diffusion-controlled intercalation and surface-redox charge storage behaviors. Energy Storage Mater. 61, 102859 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2458">39</a></sup>. Owing to the sluggish kinetics of the initial <i>c</i>-to-<i>a’</i> transformation (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#Fig5">5f</a>), the thickness of the near-surface amorphous regions is limited<sup><a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="Wei, Q. L. et al. Surface-redox sodium-ion storage in anatase titanium oxide. Nat. Commun. 14, 7 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2472">19</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 39" title="Song, G. R. et al. Physical interpretations of diffusion-controlled intercalation and surface-redox charge storage behaviors. Energy Storage Mater. 61, 102859 (2023)." href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d4928074e2475">39</a></sup>. Ex situ TEM results (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">23</a>) demonstrate the coexistence of anatase, amorphous, and electrochemically-formed RS phases in the TiO<sub>2</sub>(A)-25 nm nanoparticles after 20 cycles. Thus, TiO<sub>2</sub>(A) with larger grains delivers surface-dependent capacities and characteristic “mirror-like” CV curves after 20 cycles (Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">24</a>).</p><p>We directly assemble a TiO<sub>2</sub>(A)||Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> full cell (N/P ratio of 0.95, Supplementary Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/articles/s41467-025-57310-x#MOESM1">25a</a>) without any presodiation treatments.
